  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111602359?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780786561476" href="/book/show/7046144-the-atrocity-archives">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111602359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6787763164026737883">*This is an audio Ebook by the way. It's what I had access to through the library, but then I like audio books as well as text, at least for some fiction.*<br/><br/><br/>I'd never heard of these... they ended up on my "to be read list" because someone "here" had read them. I keep adding books faster than I can read them. (Thank you Stephen).This is actually Atrocity Archives and The Concrete Jungle in one "volume" (are Ebooks volumes?).<br/><br/>I don't know if I can accurately describe these/this books/book. The influe</span>
  <span id="freeText6787763164026737883" style="display:none">*This is an audio Ebook by the way. It's what I had access to through the library, but then I like audio books as well as text, at least for some fiction.*<br /><br /><br />I'd never heard of these... they ended up on my "to be read list" because someone "here" had read them. I keep adding books faster than I can read them. (Thank you Stephen).This is actually Atrocity Archives and The Concrete Jungle in one "volume" (are Ebooks volumes?).<br /><br />I don't know if I can accurately describe these/this books/book. The influence of H.P.Lovecraft is obvious, but that could be misleading. In a world where it's been discovered that what was accomplished "in the past" by sorcerers and sorceresses can now also be accomplished by "technology" etc. things can get, dicey. This seems to be especially true of computer "hackers", mathematicians, and other somewhat innocent techies, thinkers, geeks, and nerds. When someone accidentally stumbles on some of these "discoveries" red lights (figuratively speaking of course) go off at the "Laundry" and the person is "swept up". Generally speaking you then, agree not to go near your studies, computers etc. again...or you go to work for the Laundry. Our hero Robert, decided to work for the Laundry...<br /><br />Who are the Laundry? Well, they are the ones who keep tentacled horrors from, OUT THERE, from eating us....or our universe. There are infinite universes after all.<br /><br />Well, never mind. I like these and will continue to try and track them down. <br /><br />By the way...this is very close to a 5...I just can't quite rate it up there with some of the top rated books. Still, at least 4.5.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1769635-derek?shelf=weird-horror">weird-horror</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer752800884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3188667047973983042">Lovecraft's stories of strange angles and alterations to physics and a notion that occultism and conventional science are one and the same, separated by an ocean of knowledge beyond human scope. Stross ran with that, applying advanced mathematics and theoretical physics over the genre of weird cosmic horror. The resulting hard science fiction verisimilitude gave me the urge to reach for the nearest Wikipedia article every time a character started technical talk. And, frankly, the pinpoint detail</span>
  <span id="freeText3188667047973983042" style="display:none">Lovecraft's stories of strange angles and alterations to physics and a notion that occultism and conventional science are one and the same, separated by an ocean of knowledge beyond human scope. Stross ran with that, applying advanced mathematics and theoretical physics over the genre of weird cosmic horror. The resulting hard science fiction verisimilitude gave me the urge to reach for the nearest Wikipedia article every time a character started technical talk. And, frankly, the pinpoint detailing of <i>how</i>, <i>what</i>, and <i>why</i> gave me willies far more effectively than Lovecraft's empurpled "oh the indescribable mind-blasting horror" ever did.<br /><br />Bob Howard's modern tendency toward ironic detachment and snark seems a strange pairing with the material--Lovecraft's narrators were so damn earnest--but I came to see it as a sort of Dilbertian defense mechanism. I'm very curious to see how this series develops.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3188667047973983042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_695993293" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/695993293" />
    <a title="Wendy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4598314-wendy"><img alt="Wendy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391090778p2/4598314.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/695993293?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy" href="/user/show/4598314-wendy">Wendy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4598314-wendy?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4598314-wendy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4598314-wendy?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer695993293" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9301845769810594468">There is a list floating around Tumblr of Bioware voice actors who have narrated audiobooks. Having fallen in love with Fenris’ voice in Dragon Age II, I decided that The Atrocity Archives, read by Gideon Emery, was a necessary listen from Audible. Not that I blindly listen to an audiobook just because I want to hear sexy sweet nothings in my ear all day. The book’s blurb actually sounded interesting – though it certainly helped my enjoyment to believe that the character of Bob Howard looks exac</span>
  <span id="freeText9301845769810594468" style="display:none">There is a list floating around Tumblr of Bioware voice actors who have narrated audiobooks. Having fallen in love with Fenris’ voice in Dragon Age II, I decided that The Atrocity Archives, read by Gideon Emery, was a necessary listen from Audible. Not that I blindly listen to an audiobook just because I want to hear sexy sweet nothings in my ear all day. The book’s blurb actually sounded interesting – though it certainly helped my enjoyment to believe that the character of Bob Howard looks exactly like Fenris, if Fenris happened to be moonlighting as a snarky IT guy who works for The Laundry.<br> <br>Bob Howard is an employee at the Laundry Files, a bureaucratic organization that covertly monitors and deals with occult activities and the connections between other dimensions. He normally spends his day doing typical, mundane IT guy things, such as sorting through the messes Fred from accounting has made of his computer. Once or twice, he’s been sent out into the field, but after an unfortunate incident during an IT/Occult training course, Bob’s actions bring him to the attention of the Counter Possession Unit and leads him into doing a lot more out-of-office work.<br> <br>I really liked that Bob is not a stereotypical, introverted nerd tossed into field work where he can skillfully display his incompetence in a mock attempt at playing a geeky James Bond. Bob might need to brush up on protocol and procedure, such as what not to do when a gorgeous redheaded scientist is kidnapped, but otherwise, Bob is quite capable of handling himself in the field and is a unique character unto himself.<br> <br>For the first half, both Emery and the story kept me very entertained. Emery did an excellent job of making sure Bob’s attitude didn’t go over the edge and into the realm of unlikable characters and I loved the way Stross seamlessly worked in the occult aspects, solidly grounding them in reality through science and technology. There were a lot of technical references, but they were delivered with wit and sarcasm to make them amusing, and explained succinctly enough to make them accessible to someone as clueless about such technology as I am.<br> <br>Unfortunately, this changes in the second half, once the Atrocity Archives are discovered and the plot thickens. At this point, explanations start to take over the story as Stross works in all sorts of details about Hitler’s obsession with the occult. It is all relevant to the plot, but where previous explanations were pithy, amusing and interesting, these were tiresome, interruptive wiki entries that slowed down what should have been the action part of the novel.<br> <br>Because of this, a series that I initially expected to continue with became disappointing, though not so much so that I wouldn't allow Fenris to seduce me into reading more books in the series.<br><br>See more reviews at<br><a href="http://bibliosanctum.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The BiblioSanctum</a><br><a href="http://bibliosanctum.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347893i/702235.jpg" width="100" height="100" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9301845769810594468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_178782258" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178782258" />
    <a title="Lea" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3397530-lea"><img alt="Lea" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547050698p2/3397530.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178782258?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lea" href="/user/show/3397530-lea">Lea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3397530-lea?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3397530-lea?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3397530-lea?shelf=acquired-2011">acquired-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3397530-lea?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178782258" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4894668906315642760">Ugh.<br/><br/>I hate when a book has the most amazing, incredible, awesome idea . . . then doesn't really live up to its promise.<br/><br/>That is definitely the situation with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/101869.The_Atrocity_Archives__Laundry_Files___1_' title='The Atrocity Archives (Laundry Files, #1) by Charles Stross' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Atrocity Archives</a>. <br/><br/>The idea is kind of James Bond meets Cthulhu, but it just didn't work for me. I think the biggest problem was all the hype about how FUNNY this book is -- TECHNICAL (like, so technical I had to literally skim pages just to finish the damn thing), yes. Funny? Not so much. Unless griping about your boss is funny, somehow</span>
  <span id="freeText4894668906315642760" style="display:none">Ugh.<br /><br />I hate when a book has the most amazing, incredible, awesome idea . . . then doesn't really live up to its promise.<br /><br />That is definitely the situation with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/101869.The_Atrocity_Archives__Laundry_Files___1_" title="The Atrocity Archives (Laundry Files, #1) by Charles Stross" rel="nofollow noopener">The Atrocity Archives</a>. <br /><br />The idea is kind of James Bond meets Cthulhu, but it just didn't work for me. I think the biggest problem was all the hype about how FUNNY this book is -- TECHNICAL (like, so technical I had to literally skim pages just to finish the damn thing), yes. Funny? Not so much. Unless griping about your boss is funny, somehow, in 2012 . . .<br /><br />I saw this actually compared to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/142296.The_Anubis_Gates" title="The Anubis Gates by Tim Powers" rel="nofollow noopener">The Anubis Gates</a> in another review -- uh, NO WAY. Where that book is a mind bending mix of genres and ideas, topped off by exquisite writing, this book is what you'd get if you took the WORST of Tim Powers and mixed it with the worst of the spy genre. Just not good.<br /><br />It really surprises me how much people love this book?!<br /><br />Unfortunately, I was so taken with the IDEA of this book that I immediately bought everything in this series before reading it -- so I guess at some point I will be reading more of Stross's quasi-Lovecraftian world. Definitely not any time soon, though. I certainly hope they're better than this one.<br /><br />For a WELL written, extremely witty (literally made me laugh out loud) take on spies and Cthulhu, I'd recommend finding a copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6836828.Bump_in_the_Night" title="Bump in the Night by Tim Mulcahy" rel="nofollow noopener">Bump in the Night</a> and checking out the amazing "Ghoulspeak". I wish THIS was a multi-book series -- I'd devour them all in a single sitting!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4894668906315642760" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1320123278" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1320123278" />
    <a title="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4702933-mrsjoseph-grouchy"><img alt="MrsJoseph *grouchy*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475772748p2/4702933.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1320123278" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12736930228014969419"><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://bookslifewine.com/r-the-atrocity-archives/'>http://bookslifewine.com/r-the-atroci...</a><br/><br/><br/> <br/><br/>Note: This review is for <em>The Atrocity Archive</em> - the short story included in the book "The Concrete Jungle" will be reviewed separately.<br/><br/>How can I describe <em>The Atrocity Archive</em>? What I've been telling people thus far is to imagine Sheldon from <a href='http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0898266/?ref_=fn_al_tt_1' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Big Bang Theory</a>, take away his tendency to be completely insulting, turn him into a hacker and then force him to become the sci-fi version of a secret spy.<br/><br/>I can't quite say I enjoyed my read of <em>The Atrocity Archiv</em></span>
  <span id="freeText12736930228014969419" style="display:none"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bookslifewine.com/r-the-atrocity-archives/">http://bookslifewine.com/r-the-atroci...</a><br /><br /><br /> <br /><br />Note: This review is for <em>The Atrocity Archive</em> - the short story included in the book "The Concrete Jungle" will be reviewed separately.<br /><br />How can I describe <em>The Atrocity Archive</em>? What I've been telling people thus far is to imagine Sheldon from <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0898266/?ref_=fn_al_tt_1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Big Bang Theory</a>, take away his tendency to be completely insulting, turn him into a hacker and then force him to become the sci-fi version of a secret spy.<br /><br />I can't quite say I enjoyed my read of <em>The Atrocity Archive</em>. It was...often bogged down by what I've been calling "techno-babble." Stross clearly wrote <em>The Atrocity Archive</em> for people who are very knowledgeable in the practical application of advanced technology/mathematics. Or he was making crap up out of whole cloth. Either or.<br /><br /><br />Read the rest here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bookslifewine.com/r-the-atrocity-archives/">http://bookslifewine.com/r-the-atroci...</a><br /></span>

<div id="review_40549778" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/40549778" />
    <a title="Ron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/957848-ron"><img alt="Ron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442464391p2/957848.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/40549778?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ron" href="/user/show/957848-ron">Ron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957848-ron?shelf=mindblowing">mindblowing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957848-ron?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957848-ron?shelf=dark-humor">dark-humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957848-ron?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957848-ron?shelf=magickal">magickal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957848-ron?shelf=pulp-fiction">pulp-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957848-ron?shelf=hackers">hackers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957848-ron?shelf=disturbing">disturbing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/957848-ron?shelf=espionage">espionage</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer40549778" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4736580977239849526">Starting from an absolutely brilliant premise -- that there's a point where higher mathematics and Lovecraftian monsters meet, and computer hackers are as likely to tap into that realm as sorcerors -- Charles Stross digs deep into the bureaucracy of intelligence operations to come up with one of the niftiest plotlines about left-over Nazi occultism ever. Sensitive readers may be offended by some of the interpretations Stross gives to the Third Reich's activities, but other than that this is an e</span>
  <span id="freeText4736580977239849526" style="display:none">Starting from an absolutely brilliant premise -- that there's a point where higher mathematics and Lovecraftian monsters meet, and computer hackers are as likely to tap into that realm as sorcerors -- Charles Stross digs deep into the bureaucracy of intelligence operations to come up with one of the niftiest plotlines about left-over Nazi occultism ever. Sensitive readers may be offended by some of the interpretations Stross gives to the Third Reich's activities, but other than that this is an entertaining multilayered romp through several pop fiction traditions at once.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4736580977239849526" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1464875947" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1464875947" />
    <a title="Arun Divakar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2747498-arun-divakar"><img alt="Arun Divakar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1253201408p2/2747498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1464875947?book_show_action=true">Dec 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arun Divakar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arun Divakar" href="/user/show/2747498-arun-divakar">Arun Divakar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1464875947" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12413665370223802173">Math and I never got along right from childhood. All of the computations, formulas and details kept flying all around me and I was terribly afraid of the math teacher. But much more importantly : what the hell did it matter if sin θ/ cos θ = tan θ ? No one answered that question for me and as time went by I figured out that most of us mere humans go to the grave having never used trigonometry in real life. Mr. Charles Stross, if I had read your book in high school days and bought your theory tha</span>
  <span id="freeText12413665370223802173" style="display:none">Math and I never got along right from childhood. All of the computations, formulas and details kept flying all around me and I was terribly afraid of the math teacher. But much more importantly : what the hell did it matter if sin θ/ cos θ = tan θ ? No one answered that question for me and as time went by I figured out that most of us mere humans go to the grave having never used trigonometry in real life. Mr. Charles Stross, if I had read your book in high school days and bought your theory that mathematics can be closely approximated to magic then I wouldn’t have had to dread my math teachers ! You make a very convincing argument there though.<br /><br />Welcome to England ladies and gents, we are pleased to introduce you to a governmental agency which shall henceforth be known as ‘the laundry’. They protect you from the dangers of the occult and to borrow from the immortal words of Professor Trevor Bruttenholm (from an unrelated series) –<i> ‘There are things that go bump in the night and these are the guys who bump back’</i>. They are not handgun totting, macho, muscular alpha-males and not much of heroes either. Most of them are overworked and underpaid government employees who have a genius level grasp of science and mathematics and use these as their tools to ply their trade. The most realistic part of this story is the fact that they have to do all these while working in a plainly corporate environment. Which means : you have to enter your timesheets regularly, you have to attend the mandatory training sessions ( no matter how soporific they get), you have come squeaky clean in audits, you have to deal with impossible supervisors and also juggle your life within the labyrinths of matrix management. In short, if you try playing a hero you would be filing an unemployment claim faster than you can think. Robert Howard is a low level programmer in the service who is dying for a field assignment and the two stories in the book – The atrocity archives and The concrete jungle are his ways of growing up into a competent agent. <br /><br />This book will not have much meaning to you unless you are a passably OK nerd. If you cannot link the protagonist’s name to Conan the Barbarian and if you cannot connect his boss – Angleton’s name to a legend in the CIA then these stories will appear meaningless to you. I had to skip over a lot of technical and mathematical jargon but that did not bring down the fun factor. The author cites Len Deighton and H.P. Lovecraft as his influences and it reflects very well on the writing. The human drama in the running of an office and reckoning with forces beyond human comprehension are both extremely crucial elements by way of storytelling here.<br /><br />Recommended if you are a nerd ! Even if you are not, give it a shot. You never know, it might amuse you enough to finish the entire thing.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12413665370223802173" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RaHFN0P3ET1BFjWTV8GSG3EPfvRbz/mgBo5VB2IUzB/GKIUBHIj/q2SQEMlY/i2uh64mz3q4BwnmmpQz3BNJNw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('f7XQjeT24AiQex9f7rwksPv7KMLC6TGx05lLO9SD8uj8PJC7u4kOnrX9OgXhg5sFDVpw+eOezxgzjYoPaoR3wA==')})
  }
//]]>

His works range from science fiction and Lovecraftian horror to fantasy.<br/><br/>Stross is sometimes regarded as being part of a new generation of British science fiction writers who specialise in hard science fiction and space opera. His contemporaries include Alastair Reynolds, Ken MacLeod, Liz Williams and Richard Morgan. <br/><br/>SF</span>
